Keynesโs economic writings, including all his books, many of his published essays and articles, and a large proportion of his 
hitherto unpublished correspondence, have been published in thirty volumes by Macmillan in conjunction with the Royal Economic 
Society as [3mThe Collected Writings of John Maynard Keynes [0m(1971โ89), ed. Elizabeth Johnson and Donald Moggridge. Most of his 
private papers remain unpublished and, together with the originals of the published materials in the [3mCollected Writings [0m, are 
deposited at Kingโs College, Cambridge. The following abbreviations are used for Keynesโs work: 

[3mCW: The Collected Writings of John Maynard Keynes. [0m

[3mGT: The General Theory of Employment, Interest, and Money. [0m

[3mKP: [0mKeynes Papers. 

[3mRymes: Keynesโs Lectures, 1932โ35: [0mnotes of a representative student, transcribed, edited, and constructed by Thomas K. Rymes 
(1989).

There have been five biographers of Keynes: Roy Harrod, [3mThe Life of John Maynard Keynes [0m(1951); Charles Hession, [3mJohn Maynard 
Keynes [0m(1984); D. Moggridge, [3mMaynard Keynes: An Economistโs Biography [0m(1992); Paul Davidson, [3mJohn Maynard Keynes [0m(2007); and R. 
Skidelsky, [3mJohn Maynard Keynes: Hopes Betrayed 1883โ1920 [0m(1983), and [3mJohn Maynard Keynes: The Economist as Saviour 1920โ1937 [0m
(1992), and [3mJohn Maynard Keynes, Fighting for Britain 1937โ1946 [0m(2001). A single-volume abridgment, [3mJohn Maynard Keynes: 
Economist, Philosopher Statesman 1883โ1946 [0m, was published in 2003. Skidelskyโs [3mKeynes: The Return of the Master [0m(2009) was a plea 
for his relevance to understand, and prescribe for, the slump of 2008-9. Anand Chandavarkar, [3mThe Unexplored Keynes and Other 
Essays [0m(2009) offers an engaging account of Keynesโs many-sided genius. Justyn Walsh, [3mKeynes and the Market [0m(2008) shows how 
Keynesโs varied experience as an investor influenced his economic theories. 

[1mุงููุธุฑูุฉ [0m

Only a tiny sample of a vast secondary literature can be given here. Paul Krugman, [3mIntroduction to Keynesโs The General Theory of 
Employment, Interest and Money [0m(2006) is a scintillating account of Keynesโs central theory from a โnew Keynesianโ standpoint. 
Michael Stewart, [3mKeynes and After [0m(3rd edn. 1986), is the most accessible introductory text. E. Eshag, [3mFrom Marshall to Keynes: An 
Essay on the Monetary Theory of the Cambridge School [0m(1963), the classic account, needs to be supplemented by R. J. Bigg, [3m
Cambridge and the Monetary Theory of Production [0m(1990). D. Patinkin, [3mKeynesโs Monetary Thought: A Study of its Development [0m(1977), 
as well as his essay on Keynes in the [3mNew Palgrave Dictionary of Economics [0m, ed. J. Eatwell, M. Milgate, and P. Newman (1987), are 
standard technical accounts. J. R. Hicksโs [3mCritical Essays in Monetary Theory [0m(1967) has an illuminating โNote on the Treatise (on 
Money)โ. Richard Kahn, [3mThe Making of Keynesโs General Theory [0m(1984), is important first-hand testimony; G. L. S. Shackle, [3mThe 
Years of High Theory: Invention and Tradition in Economic Thought 1926โ39 [0m(1967), is an excellent account of the โdouble 
revolutionโ in Cambridge. Four stimulating interpretations of Keynesโs theory are Tim Congdon, [3mKeynes, the Keynesians, and 
Monetarism [0m(2007); Gilles Dostaler, [3mKeynes and His Battles [0m(2007); A. H. Meltzer, [3mKeynesโs Monetary Theory: A Different 
Interpretation [0m(1988); and Murray Milgate, [3mCapital and Employment: A Study of Keynesโs Economics [0m(1982). Victoria Chick, [3mOn Money, 
Method and Keynes: Selected Essays [0m, ed. Philip Arestis and Sheila Dow (1992), and Hyman P. Minsky, [3mJohn Maynard Keynes [0m(1975) are 
important interpretations from the post-Keynesian standpoint. P. Clarke, [3mThe Keynesian Revolution in the Making 1924โ1936 [0m(1988) 
is essential reading; R. W. Dimand, [3mThe Origins of the Keynesian Revolution [0m(1988) covers some of the same ground from a technical 
standpoint. P. V. Mini, [3mKeynes, Bloomsbury and The General Theory [0m(1991) is a stimulating, off-beat essay. John Williamsonโs 
essay, โKeynes and the International Economic Orderโ, in D. Worswick and J. Trevithik (eds.), [3mKeynes and the Modern World [0m(1983) 
is exemplary. Indispensable introductions to Keynesโs epistemology are Anna M. Carabelli, [3mOn Keynesโs Method [0m(1988) and R. M. 
OโDonnell, [3mKeynes: Philosophy, Economics and Politics [0m(1989). Terence Hutchison, [3mOn the Methodology of Economics and the Formalist 
Revolution [0m(2000) is an excellent account of how economics came to be โmathematicizedโ. Taleb Nassim, [3mThe Black Swan: The Impact 
of the Highly Improbable [0m(2007) shows up the fraudulence of most mathematical forecasting models. 

[1mููุฑุงุซ ูููุฒ [0m

D. Patinkin, [3mMoney, Interest and Prices: An Integration of Monetary and Value Theory [0m(1956), and the Hicks-Patinkin exchange which 
followed it in the [3mEconomic Journal [0m(June 1957 and September 1959), were key to establishing the โsynthesisโ between the 
neo-classical theorists and the policy Keynesians; an accommodation challenged by A. Leijonhufvud, [3mOn Keynesian Economics and the 
Economics of Keynes [0m(1966). (See also Leijonhufvudโs essay, [3mKeynes and the Classics [0m(Institute of Economic Affairs, 1969).) David 
Marquand, [3mThe Unprincipled Society [0m(1988) offers a lively interpretation of โKeynesian social democracyโ in Britain; for the 
impact of Keynesian ideas in the United States, H. Stein, [3mThe Fiscal Revolution in America [0m(1969) is the key text; for Keynesโs 
influence on other countries, see Peter A. Hall (ed.), [3mThe Political Power of Economic Ideas: Keynesianism Across Nations [0m(1989). 
Eric Roll, [3mThe World After Keynes: An Examination of the Economic Order [0m(1968) is a standard offering from the โgolden ageโ. The 
crucial monetarist text is Milton Friedmanโs Presidential address to the American Economic Association, 29 December 1967, on โThe 
Role of Monetary Policyโ, published in the [3mAmerican Economic Review [0m(March 1968), 1โ17. The main text of โnew Keynesianismโ is N. 
G. Mankiw and D. Romer (eds.), [3mNew Keynesian Economics [0m(1991). Paul Davidsonโs [3mMoney and the Real World [0m(2002 edition) is the 
statement of one of the leading โpost-Keynesiansโ. Henry Hazlitt (ed.), [3mThe Critics of Keynesian Economics [0m(1960, 1977) is a 
collection of anti-Keynesian and sceptical essays. Arjo Klamer, [3mThe New Classical Macroeconomics: Conversations with New Classical 
Economists and Their Opponents [0m(1984) is an indispensable window into the mindset of the Chicago School. Brian Snowdon and Howard 
R. Vane, [3mModern Macroeconomics: Its Origins, Development and Current State [0m(2005) charts the โdecline and fallโ of the original 
Keynesian revolution, and the rise of โnew Keynesianismโ and the โnew classical economicsโ, with interviews with some of the 
leading participants.
